data-twitter-account="CNN" data-image-src="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/160624120538-lgbt-national-monument-stonewall-nccorig-00004301-super-tease.jpg"></div><div js-pg-rail-tall__head"><section class="zn zn-large-media zn-body zn--idx-0 zn--ordinary zn-has-one-container" data-eq-pts="xsmall: 0, medium: 460, large: 780, full16x9: 1100" id="large-media" data-vr-zone="zone-0-0" data-zone-label="headerMedia" data-containers="1" id="large-media" data-zn-id="large-media"><div class="l-container"><img class="media__image media__image--responsive" alt="Supporters of same-sex marriages gather outside the US Supreme Court waiting for its decision on April 28, 2015, in Washington." data-src-mini="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/150428113819-scotus-gay-marriage-small-169.jpg" data-src-xsmall="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/150428113819-scotus-gay-marriage-medium-plus-169.jpg" data-src-small="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/150428113819-scotus-gay-marriage-large-169.jpg" data-src-medium="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/150428113819-scotus-gay-marriage-exlarge-169.jpg" data-src-large="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/150428113819-scotus-gay-marriage-super-169.jpg" data-src-full16x9="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/150428113819-scotus-gay-marriage-full-169.jpg" data-src-mini1x1="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/150428113819-scotus-gay-marriage-small-11.jpg"  data-demand-load="not-loaded" data-eq-pts="mini: 0,  xsmall: 221,  small: 308,  medium: 461,  large:  781" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhEAAJAJEAAAAAAP///////wAAACH5BAEAAAIALAAAAAAQAAkAAAIKlI+py+0Po5yUFQA7"><div class="img__preloader"></div><noscript><img alt="Supporters of same-sex marriages gather outside the US Supreme Court waiting for its decision on April 28, 2015, in Washington." class="media__image" src="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/150428113819-scotus-gay-marriage-large-169.jpg"></noscript><div class="media__caption el__gallery_image-title"><div class="element-raw appearance-standard">Supporters of same-sex marriages gather outside the US Supreme Court waiting for its decision on April 28, 2015, in Washington.</div></div></div></section></div><div class="pg-rail-tall__body" itemprop="articleBody"><section class="zn zn-body-text zn-body zn--idx-0 zn--ordinary zn-has-multiple-containers zn-has-78-containers" data-eq-pts="xsmall: 0, medium: 460, large: 780, full16x9: 1100" id="body-text" data-vr-zone="zone-1-0" data-zone-label="bodyText" data-containers="78" id="body-text" data-zn-id="body-text"><div class="l-container"><div class="el__leafmedia el__leafmedia--sourced-paragraph"><p class="zn-body__paragraph"><cite class="el-editorial-source"> (CNN)</cite>Here is some background information about lesbian, gay, bisexual and transgender milestones in the United States.</p></div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong><u>Timeline:</strong></u><strong><br />1924 - </strong>The<a href="http://www.pbs.org/wgbh/americanexperience/features/timeline/stonewall/" target="_blank"> Society for Human Rights</a> is founded by Henry Gerber in Chicago. It is the first documented gay rights organization.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>1950 - </strong>The Mattachine Society is formed by activist Harry Hay and is one of the first sustained gay rights groups in the United States. The Society focuses on social acceptance and other support for homosexuals.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>April 1952 -</strong> The American Psychiatric Association's diagnostic manual lists homosexuality as a <a href="http://psychology.ucdavis.edu/faculty_sites/rainbow/html/facts_mental_health.html" target="_blank">sociopathic personality disturbance</a>.</div><div class="ad ad--epic ad--mobile" data-ad-text="show"><div id="ad_rect_atf_02" class="ad-ad_rect_atf_02 ad-refresh-default"></div></div><div class="ad ad--epic ad--tablet" data-ad-text="show"><div id="ad_rect_atf_02" class="ad-ad_rect_atf_02 ad-refresh-default"></div></div><div class="ad ad--epic ad--desktop" data-ad-text="show"><div id="ad_rect_atf_02" class="ad-ad_rect_atf_02 ad-refresh-default"></div></div><ul class="cn cn-list-hierarchical-xs cn--idx-5 cn-zoneAdContainer"></ul><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>April 27, 1953 - </strong>President Dwight D. Eisenhower signs an <a href="http://www.archives.gov/federal-register/codification/executive-order/10450.html" target="_blank">executive order </a>that bans homosexuals from working for the federal government, saying they are a security risk.</div><div class="zn-body__read-more"><div class="read-more-gradient"></div><div class="read-more-button"><div class="read-more-link" id="js-body-read-more">Read More</div></div></div><div class="zn-body__read-all"><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>September 1955 - </strong>The first known lesbian rights organization in the United States forms in San Francisco. Daughters of Bilitis (DOB). They host private social functions, fearing police raids, threats of violence and discrimination in bars and clubs. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>July 1961 -</strong> Illinois becomes the first state to <a href="http://articles.chicagotribune.com/1989-06-26/news/8902120553_1_gay-bar-anti-gay-activists-first-openly-gay-supervisor" target="_blank">decriminalize homosexuality</a> by repealing their sodomy laws.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>September 11, 1961 - </strong>The first <a href="https://diva.sfsu.edu/collections/sfbatv/bundles/225539" target="_blank">US televised documentary about homosexuality</a> airs on a local station in California.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>June 28, 1969 - </strong>Police raid the <a href="http://www.thestonewallinnnyc.com/StonewallInnNYC/HISTORY.html" target="_blank">Stonewall Inn in New York City</a>. Protests and demonstrations begin, and it later becomes known as the impetus for the gay civil rights movement in the United States.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>1969 -</strong> <a href="http://www.advocate.com/arts-entertainment/advocate-45/2012/03/28/part-5-our-hall-fame?page=0" target="_blank">The "Los Angeles Advocate," founded in 1967,</a> is renamed "The Advocate." It is considered the oldest continuing LGBT publication that began as a newsletter published by the activist group Personal Rights in Defense and Education (PRIDE).</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>1970s -</strong> The<a href="http://www.ushmm.org/wlc/en/article.php?ModuleId=10005378" target="_blank"> Pink Triangle</a> becomes a symbol of gay pride after being used during <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/07/09/world/world-war-ii-fast-facts/index.html">World War II </a>as a symbol of homosexuality, perversion and deviance. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>June 28, 1970 - </strong>Community members in New York City march through the local streets to recognize the one-year anniversary of the Stonewall riots. This event is named <a href="http://www.pbs.org/wgbh/americanexperience/features/timeline/stonewall/" target="_blank">Christopher Street Liberation Day</a>, and is now considered the first gay pride parade.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>1973 - <a href="http://wabe.org/post/georgians-react-supreme-court-s-gay-marriage-ruling" target="_blank"></strong>Lambda Legal</a> becomes the first legal organization established to fight for the equal rights of gays and lesbians. Lambda also becomes their own first client after being denied non-profit status; the New York Supreme Court eventually rules that Lambda Legal can exist as a non-profit.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>January 1, 1973 - <a href="http://www.ncsl.org/research/human-services/same-sex-marriage-laws.aspx" target="_blank"></strong>Maryland</a> becomes the first state to statutorily ban <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/05/28/us/same-sex-marriage-fast-facts/index.html">same-sex marriage</a>.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>March 26, 1973 - </strong>First meeting of "<a href="http://community.pflag.org/page.aspx?pid=191" target="_blank">Parents and Friends of Gays,"</a> which goes national as Parents, Families and Friends of Lesbians and Gays (PFLAG) in 1982.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>December 15, 1973 - </strong>By a vote of 5,854 to 3,810,<a href="http://www.apa.org/helpcenter/sexual-orientation.aspx" target="_blank"> the American Psychiatric Association removes homosexuality</a> from its list of mental disorders in the DSM-II Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>1974 -</strong> <a href="http://www.pbs.org/wgbh/americanexperience/features/timeline/stonewall/" target="_blank">Kathy Kozachenko becomes the first openly LGBT American elected to any public office</a> when she wins a seat on the Ann Arbor, Michigan City Council. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>1974 -</strong> <a href="http://theadvocatemag.tumblr.com/post/114055171094/elaine-noble-the-first-openly-gay-or-lesbian" target="_blank">Elaine Noble is the first openly gay candidate elected </a>to a state office when she is elected to the Massachusetts State legislature. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>January 14, 1975 - </strong>The<a href="https://www.congress.gov/bill/94th-congress/house-bill/166/all-info" target="_blank"> first federal gay rights bill</a> is introduced to address discrimination based on sexual orientation. The bill later goes to the Judiciary Committee but is never brought for consideration. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>March 1975 - </strong>Technical Sergeant Leonard P. Matlovich reveals his sexual orientation to his commanding officer and is forcibly discharged from the Air Force six months later. Matlovich is a <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/07/01/world/vietnam-war-fast-facts/index.html">Vietnam War</a> veteran and was awarded both the Purple Heart and the Bronze Star. In 1980, the Court of Appeals rules that the dismissal was improper. Matlovich is awarded his back pay and a retroactive promotion. Upon his death, the inscription on his gravestone read: <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/1988/06/24/us/gay-airman-who-fought-ouster-dies-from-aids.html" target="_blank">''When I was in the military they gave me a medal for killing two men and a discharge for loving one.''</a></div><div class="el__embedded el__embedded--standard"><div class="el__gallery--standard js__gallery--standard js__leafmedia--gallery"><div class="js__gallery__close--standard el__gallery__close--standard el__storyelements--close"></div><div class="el__gallery--teaseimage"><div class="el__resize"><div class="el__position media js-gallery-aspect-ratio-wrapper"><img class="media__image media__image--responsive media__image--cut-format" alt="It was rare for black models like Tracey &amp;quot;Africa&amp;quot; Norman to break into the cutthroat lily-white world of modeling in the 1970s. Norman, who had exclusive contracts for Avon skin care and Clairol&amp;#39;s Born Beautiful hair color, didn&amp;#39;t tell anyone she was also transgender and had been born male. Once her secret was out, the work dried up. Here are some other notable moments in the recent history of transgender identity." data-src-mini="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/151216101744-tracey-africa-norman-small-169.jpg" data-src-xsmall="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/151216101744-tracey-africa-norman-medium-plus-169.jpg" data-src-small="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/151216101744-tracey-africa-norman-large-169.jpg" data-src-medium="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/151216101744-tracey-africa-norman-exlarge-169.jpg" data-src-large="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/151216101744-tracey-africa-norman-super-169.jpg" data-src-full16x9="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/151216101744-tracey-africa-norman-full-169.jpg" data-src-mini1x1="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/151216101744-tracey-africa-norman-small-11.jpg"  data-demand-load="not-loaded" data-eq-pts="mini: 0,  xsmall: 221,  small: 308,  medium: 461,  large:  781" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhEAAJAJEAAAAAAP///////wAAACH5BAEAAAIALAAAAAAQAAkAAAIKlI+py+0Po5yUFQA7" data-cut-format="16:9"><div class="img__preloader"></div><noscript><img alt="It was rare for black models like Tracey &amp;quot;Africa&amp;quot; Norman to break into the cutthroat lily-white world of modeling in the 1970s. Norman, who had exclusive contracts for Avon skin care and Clairol&amp;#39;s Born Beautiful hair color, didn&amp;#39;t tell anyone she was also transgender and had been born male. Once her secret was out, the work dried up. Here are some other notable moments in the recent history of transgender identity." class="media__image" src="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/151216101744-tracey-africa-norman-super-169.jpg"></noscript><div class="media__icon icon-media-gallery"></div></div></div><div class="js-media__caption media__caption el__storyelement__title"><div class="element-raw appearance-standard"><span class=el__storyelement__header> Photos:</span> <span class=el__storyelement__gray>Transgender identity in the news</span></div></div></div><div class="el-carousel__wrapper"><div class=" js-owl-carousel owl-carousel carousel--full body" data-galleryname="Transgender identity in the news" data-cut-format="16:9" data-is-gallery="true" data-slide-count="17"><div data-slidename="Transgender identity in the news" data-analytics="_body_image"><div class="el__resize"><div class="el__position media js-gallery-aspect-ratio-wrapper"><img class="media__image media__image--responsive media__image--cut-format" alt="It was rare for black models like Tracey &amp;quot;Africa&amp;quot; Norman to break into the cutthroat lily-white world of modeling in the 1970s. class="js-el__gallery-caption el__gallery-caption">Hide Caption</div><div class="el__gallery-photocount"> 17 of 17</div></div></div></div><div class="owl-carousel js-owl-filmstrip owl-filmstrip" ><img src="//i2.cdn.cnn.com/cnnnext/dam/assets/150314140353-jazz-jennings-2013-small-11.jpg" alt="jazz jennings 2013" /></div><div class="ad-slide--inactive ad-slide js-ad-slide"><div class="ad-slide__prev"></div><div class="ad-slide__next"></div></div><script>/* global CNN */'use strict';jQuery(document).ready(function () {var galleryAdSlide = new CNN.AdSlide('el__gallery', false, CNN.contentModel.singletonFile);});</script></div></div></div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>1976 -</strong> After undergoing gender reassignment surgery in 1975, ophthalmologist and professional tennis player Renee Richards is banned from competing in the women's <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/07/31/us/u-s-open-tennis-tournament-fast-facts/index.html" target="_blank">US Open</a> because of a "women-born-women" rule. Richards challenges the decision and in 1977, the New York Supreme Court rules in her favor. Richards competes in the 1977 US Open but is defeated in the first round by Virginia Wade.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>May 24, 1976 -</strong> <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/books/2014/jan/31/tales-city-armistead-maupin-damian-barr" target="_blank">"Tales of the City," by Armistead Maupin</a> appears in the San Francisco Chronicle. It is among the first fiction works to address a disease that initially affected gay men (it would later be identified as <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/07/29/health/aids-hiv-fast-facts/index.html">AIDS</a>), and feature many minority characters and homosexual relationships.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>1977-1981 - </strong>Billy Crystal plays one of the first openly gay characters in a recurring role on a prime time television show in "Soap."</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>January 9, 1978 - <a href="http://milkfoundation.org/about/harvey-milk-biography/" target="_blank"></strong>Harvey Milk is inaugurated as San Francisco city supervisor,</a> and is the first openly gay man to be elected to a political office in California. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>1978 - </strong>Inspired by Harvey Milk to develop a symbol of pride and hope for the LGBT community, <a href="http://www.sanfrancisco.travel/article/brief-history-rainbow-flag" target="_blank">Gilbert Baker designs and stitches together the first rainbow flag.</a></div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>November 27, 1978 -<a href="http://www.sfgate.com/news/article/CITY-HALL-SLAYINGS-25-Years-Later-Revisiting-2510798.php" target="_blank"><strong></strong> </strong>Harvey Milk and Mayor George Moscone are murdered </a>by Dan White, who had recently resigned from his San Francisco board position and wanted Moscone to reappoint him. White later serves just over five years in prison for voluntary manslaughter.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>October 14, 1979 -</strong> The first National<a href="http://www.glbtq.com/social-sciences/marches_washington.html" target="_blank"> March on Washington for Lesbian and Gay Rights</a> takes place. It draws an estimated 75,000 to 125,000 individuals marching for LGBT rights.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>March 2, 1982 - </strong>Wisconsin becomes the first state to outlaw discrimination based on sexual orientation.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>1983 -</strong> Lambda Legal wins People v. West 12 Tenants Corp., the first HIV/AIDS discrimination lawsuit. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>December 1, 1988 - </strong>The World Health Organization holds the first <a href="http://www.worldaidsday.org/" target="_blank">World AIDS Day</a> in order to raise awareness.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>November 30, 1993 - <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/02/01/us/bill-clinton-fast-facts/index.html"></strong>President Bill Clinton </a>signs a <a href="http://dont.law.stanford.edu/wp-content/uploads/2010/11/extract-1332_14-jan281982.pdf" target="_blank">military policy</a> directive that prohibits openly gay and lesbian Americans from serving in the military, but also prohibits the harassment of "closeted" homosexuals. The policy is known as "Don't Ask, Don't Tell."</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>1994 - </strong>The movie "Philadelphia," depicting a closeted gay man dying of AIDS, wins two <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/08/09/us/academy-awards-fast-facts/index.html">Academy Awards</a>.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>November 1995 - </strong>The <a href="https://www.congress.gov/bill/103rd-congress/house-bill/1152" target="_blank">Hate Crimes Sentencing Enhancement Act</a> goes into effect as part of the Violent Crime Control and Law Enforcement Act of 1994. The law allows a judge to impose harsher sentences if there is evidence showing that a victim was selected because of the "actual or perceived race, color, religion, national origin, ethnicity, gender, disability, or sexual orientation of any person."</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>September 21, 1996 -</strong> President Bill Clinton signs the <a href="http://www.gpo.gov/fdsys/pkg/PLAW-104publ199/pdf/PLAW-104publ199.pdf" target="_blank">Defense of Marriage Act,</a> banning federal recognition of same-sex marriage and defining marriage as "a legal union between one man and one woman as husband and wife."</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>December 3, 1996 -</strong> <a href="http://people.umass.edu/~leg450/Cases%20and%20statutes/BaehrvMiike.pdf" target="_blank">Hawaii's Judge Chang rules that the state does not have a legal right to deprive same-sex couples of the right to marry</a>, making Hawaii the first state to recognize that gay and lesbian couples are entitled to the same privileges as heterosexual married couples.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>April 1997 - </strong>Comedian <a href="http://www.cnn.com/SHOWBIZ/9704/06/ellen/">Ellen DeGeneres</a> comes out as a lesbian on the cover Time magazine, stating, <a href="http://content.time.com/time/covers/0,16641,19970414,00.html" target="_blank">"Yep, I'm Gay."</a></div><div class="el__embedded el__embedded--standard"><div class="el__gallery--standard class="ad-slide__prev"></div><div class="ad-slide__next"></div></div><script>/* global CNN */'use strict';jQuery(document).ready(function () {var galleryAdSlide = new CNN.AdSlide('el__gallery', false, CNN.contentModel.singletonFile);});</script></div></div></div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>April 30, 1997 -</strong> Ellen DeGeneres' character, Ellen Morgan on her self-titled TV series "Ellen," becomes the first leading character to come out on a prime time network television show.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>April 1, 1998 - <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/01/17/us/martin-luther-king-jr-fast-facts/index.html"></strong>Martin Luther King, Jr.'s</a> widow,<a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/08/23/us/coretta-scott-king-fast-facts/index.html"> Coretta Scott King</a>, asks the civil rights community to help in the effort to extinguish homophobia.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>October 6-7, 1998 - <a href="http://www.cnn.com/US/9810/16/shepard.funeral.03/"></strong>Matthew Shepard </a>is tied to a fence, beaten and left to die near Laramie, Wyoming. He is eventually found by a cyclist, who initially mistakes him for a scarecrow.  </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>October 9, 1998 - </strong>Russell Henderson and Aaron McKinney from Laramie, Wyoming, make their first court appearance after being arrested for the attempted murder of Matthew Shepard. Eventually, they each receive two life sentences for killing Shepard.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>October 12, 1998 -</strong> Matthew Shepard dies from his injuries sustained in the beating.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>April 26, 2000 - </strong>Vermont being comes the first state to legalize civil-unions between same-sex couples.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>June 2003 - </strong>The US Supreme Court strikes down the "homosexual conduct" law, which decriminalizes same-sex sexual conduct, with their opinion in Lawrence v. Texas. The decision also reverses Bowers v. Hardwick, a 1986 US Supreme Court ruling that upheld Georgia's sodomy law.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>May 17, 2004 - </strong>The first legal same-sex marriage in the United States occurs in Massachusetts.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>September 6, 2005 - </strong>The California legislature becomes the first to pass a bill allowing marriage between same-sex couples. <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/08/06/us/arnold-schwarzenegger-fast-facts/index.html">Governor Arnold Schwarzenegger</a> vetoes the bill.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>December 9, 2005 - <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2005/SHOWBIZ/Movies/09/12/brokeback.toronto/"></strong>"Brokeback Mountain"</a> is released to limited audiences in New York, Los Angeles and San Francisco. The film, directed by Ang Lee, focuses on a love story between two men that stretches over decades, and survives in a time and place in which the two men's feelings for each other were utterly taboo. The film stars Jake Gyllenhaal and Heath Ledger, and goes on to win several <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/08/09/us/golden-globe-awards-fast-facts/index.html">Golden Globe Awards</a> and Academy Awards.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>October 25, 2006 - </strong>The<a href="http://www.cnn.com/2006/US/10/25/gay.marriage/"> New Jersey Supreme Court</a> rules that state lawmakers must provide the rights and benefits of marriage to gay and lesbian couples. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>May 15, 2008 - </strong>The California Supreme Court rules in <em>re: Marriage<em></em> Cases</em> that limiting marriage to opposite-sex couples is unconstitutional.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>November 4, 2008 - </strong>Voters approve Proposition 8 in California, which makes same-sex marriage illegal.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>February 22, 2009 - </strong>Actor Sean Penn wins an Oscar for his role as Harvey Milk in the film, "Milk." The film also won for "Best Original Screenplay."</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>August 12, 2009 - </strong>Harvey Milk is posthumously awarded the Medal of Freedom by <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2012/12/26/us/barack-obama---fast-facts/index.html">President Barack Obama</a>.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>October 28, 2009 - </strong>President Barack Obama signs the <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2009/POLITICS/10/28/hate.crimes/">Matthew Shepard and James Byrd, Jr. Hate Crimes Prevention Act</a> into law. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>August 4, 2010 - </strong>Proposition 8 is found unconstitutional by a federal judge.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>September 20, 2011 - </strong>"Don't Ask, Don't Tell" is repealed, ending a ban on gay men and lesbians from serving openly in the military. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>May 9, 2012 - </strong>In an ABC interview,<strong> </strong>Barack Obama becomes the first sitting US president to publicly support the <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2012/05/09/politics/obama-same-sex-marriage/">freedom for LGBT couples to marry.</a> </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>September 4, 2012 - </strong>The Democratic Party becomes the first major US political party in history to publicly support same-sex marriage on a national platform at the Democratic National Convention.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>November 6, 2012 - <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2012/11/07/politics/wisconsin-tammy-baldwin-senate/" target="_blank"></strong>Tammy Baldwin becomes the first</a> openly gay politician and the first Wisconsin woman, elected to the US Senate. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>June 26, 2013 -</strong> In <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/03/27/us/new-york-doma-windsor/">United States v. Windsor</a>, the <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/06/10/us/u-s-supreme-court-fast-facts/index.html">US Supreme Court</a> strikes down section 3 of the Defense of Marriage Act, ruling that legally married same-sex couples are entitled to federal benefits. The high court also dismisses a case involving California's proposition 8.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>October 6, 2014 - </strong>The United States Supreme Court denies review in five different marriage cases, allowing lower court rulings to stand, and therefore allowing same-sex couples to marry in Utah, Oklahoma, Virginia, Indiana and Wisconsin. The decision opens the door for the right to marry in Colorado, Kansas, North Carolina, South Carolina, West Virginia and Wyoming. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>June 9, 2015 - <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2014/12/11/us/ashton-carter-fast-facts/index.html"></strong>Secretary of Defense Ash Carter</a> announces that the <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2015/06/09/politics/carter-sexual-orientation-policy/index.html">Military Equal Opportunity policy has been adjusted to include gay and lesbian military members</a>. js-ad-slide"><div class="ad-slide__prev"></div><div class="ad-slide__next"></div></div><script>/* global CNN */'use strict';jQuery(document).ready(function () {var galleryAdSlide = new CNN.AdSlide('el__gallery', false, CNN.contentModel.singletonFile);});</script></div></div></div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>April 24, 2015 - </strong>In a televised interview with ABC's Diane Sawyer, US <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/10/01/world/summer-olympics-competitions-fast-facts/index.html">Olympic</a> gold medal winner Bruce Jenner says, <a href="http://money.cnn.com/2015/04/24/media/bruce-jenner-interview-diane-sawyer/">"Yes, for all intents and purposes, I'm a woman." </a>Jenner later reveals that she is now <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2015/06/01/entertainment/bruce-caitlyn-jenner-vanity-fair-feat/">Caitlyn Jenner</a> and will live as a woman.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>April 28, 2015 - <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2015/04/28/politics/supreme-court-gay-marriage-arguments/"></strong>The US Supreme Court hears oral arguments on the question of the freedom to marry</a> in Kentucky, Tennessee, Ohio and Michigan. The decision may bring a national resolution on the issue of same-sex marriage. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>June 26, 2015 -</strong> The Supreme Court rules that states cannot ban same-sex marriage. The 5-4 ruling had <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/02/22/us/anthony-kennedy-fast-facts/index.html">Justice Anthony Kennedy </a>writing for the majority with the four liberal justices. Each of the four conservative justices writes their own dissent.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>July 27, 2015 - <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2015/07/27/us/boy-scouts-gay-leaders-feat/"></strong>Boy Scouts of America</a> President <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/10/17/us/robert-gates-fast-facts/index.html">Robert Gates</a> announces "the national executive board ratified a resolution removing the national restriction on openly gay leaders and employees."</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>May 17, 2016 - <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2016/05/17/politics/eric-fanning-secretary-of-the-army/"></strong>The Senate confirms Eric Fanning to be secretary of the Army,</a> making him the first openly gay secretary of a US military branch. Fanning previously served as Defense Secretary Ash Carter's chief of staff, and also served as undersecretary of the Air Force and deputy undersecretary of the Navy.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>June 24, 2016 -</strong> <a href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/blog/2016/06/24/president-obama-designates-stonewall-national-monument" target="_blank">President Barack Obama announces the designation of the first national monument to lesbian, gay, bisexual and transgender (LGBT) rights.</a> The <a href="https://www.nps.gov/ston/index.htm" target="_blank">Stonewall National Monument</a> will encompass Christopher Park, the Stonewall Inn and the surrounding streets and sidewalks that were the sites of the 1969 Stonewall uprising. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>June 30, 2016 - </strong>Secretary of Defense Ash Carter announces that the Pentagon is <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2016/06/30/politics/transgender-ban-lifted-us-military/" target="_blank">lifting the ban on transgender people serving openly in the US military. </a>The decision removes one of the last remaining barriers to LGBT participation in the armed forces.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>August 5-21, 2016 - <a href="http://edition.cnn.com/2016/08/11/sport/rio-2016-lgbt-olympians/" target="_blank"></strong>A record number of "out" athletes compete in the summer Olympic Games in Rio de Janeiro.</a> Human Rights Campaign estimates that there are at least 41 openly lesbian, gay and bisexual Olympians -- up from 23 that participated in London 2012 -- though Outsports.com puts that number much higher at 49.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>November 9, 2016 - </strong>Kate Brown is sworn in as governor of Oregon, a day after she was officially elected to the office. Brown becomes the highest-ranking LGBT person elected to office in the United States. Brown took over the governorship in February 2016 (without an election), after Democrat John Kitzhaber resigned amidst a criminal investigation. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>January 31, 2017 - </strong>Thousands of gay and bisexual men who were convicted of now-abolished sexual offenses in Britain have been posthumously pardoned under a new policing law, <a href="https://www.gov.uk/government/news/thousands-officially-pardoned-under-turings-law" target="_blank">the Justice Ministry announces.</a> The law, which received Royal Assent on this day, is named after British WWII codebreaker Alan Turing, who committed suicide following his conviction for gross indecency and was posthumously pardoned by Her Majesty the Queen in 2013. It also makes it possible for living convicted gay men to seek pardons for offenses no longer on the statute book.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph"><strong>April 4, 2017 - <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2017/04/04/politics/lgbt-employees-appeals-court/index.html"></strong>The 7th District Court of Appeals rules that the Civil Rights Act prohibits workplace discrimination against LGBT employees</a>, after  Kimberly Hively sues Ivy Tech Community College for violating Title VII of the act by denying her employment. </div></div><p class="zn-body__paragraph
